  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_aaacf293-5fb2-4f77-b8aa-76dc40acdfee'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    <a title="Greenbear" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12544680-greenbear"><img alt="Greenbear" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346855444p2/12544680.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3224281954?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greenbear" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greenbear" href="/user/show/12544680-greenbear">Greenbear</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3224281954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12999947491743511442">TLDR: Average first half, atrocious second half.<br/><br/>The base story of "Strawberry Picker" is intriguing enough: Jette's and Merle's best friend (Caro) has a new boyfriend, who is extremely reclusive. They don't know his name or have ever met him. Then suddenly, Caro is dead, and the elusive boyfriend is the prime suspect. But how to find someone who was so close and yet left no trace?<br/>That's the good part. Everything goes downhill from there. <br/><br/>This book is plagued by two major flaws:<br/>1. The cover text </span>
  <span id="freeText12999947491743511442" style="display:none">TLDR: Average first half, atrocious second half.<br /><br />The base story of "Strawberry Picker" is intriguing enough: Jette's and Merle's best friend (Caro) has a new boyfriend, who is extremely reclusive. They don't know his name or have ever met him. Then suddenly, Caro is dead, and the elusive boyfriend is the prime suspect. But how to find someone who was so close and yet left no trace?<br />That's the good part. Everything goes downhill from there. <br /><br />This book is plagued by two major flaws:<br />1. The cover text of the book already reveals major spoilers from 2/3 of the book for some reason, so the reader knows that Jette will also fall in love with this guy. And it's boring as hell. We know who the murderer is, since the author decided to write several chapters from his perspective. There's nothing to conclude, only the ever-growing question of "Why?". <br />2. The absurdly daft main characters. I'm talking about the deceased Caro and her best friend Jette here. <br />Caro falls in love with a guy that obviously doesn't trust her enough to even give her his name. Still she believes he's the one, doesn't tell her best friends about him and even gives him a second key to her flat... the same flat she shares with her two female best friends that don't even know this guy exists! That's not even dumb anymore, that's criminal.<br />Jette picks up right where Caro left. She's supposed to be a likable detective girl, yet all I remember is her infantile whining about how much in love she is. There is exactly ONE SINGLE eye witness that could identify the ghost-like boyfriend of Caro: a waitress that gives a proper description (both physically and how he behaved) of the killer. About one day later, Jette meets a man that is the spitting image of this description and he even seems to follow her around and act in the same way Caro's boyfriend did. Naturally Jette, being a smart, young, independent woman puts two and two together, right? No. She's plain dumb and ignores all clues and her own vows to find the killer. Instead she tries to be a good wife to this stranger who is 10 years older than her and acts like a real creep. She's suspicious of every single person she encounters, even random women, even though all the victims have been raped. Even the bloody police officer who's just trying to solve the case is treated aggressively. But who get's the benefit of the doubt? The obvious killer. That's just dumb writing. <br />Without the frustratingly stupid decisions of these two girls, the book wouldn't even last for 100 pages.<br /><br />I don't understand why the eyewitness report was in the book at all. It didn't factor into the solving of the case one bit. Also, even though the killer raped all his victims and had a relationship with one of them for several weeks, there are absolutely no physical traces anywhere. No semen, no DNA, nothing. Sure, he left some clothes lying around, but there can't be any DNA on that, right? Right???<br /><br />During the last third of this book I wanted to scream at the protagonists so badly. So no, don't read this if you have any alternative. It's just not a good book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12999947491743511442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10478024610016151754">This was the first novel I've ever read in entirety in German so I was pretty proud of myself for that. However, it wasn't as good as I was hoping it would be. The back cover basically gives away the first 220 pages (of a 350 page book), so it was hard to get through the first 50% of the book already knowing what was going to happen.   <span id="freeText10478024610016151754" style="display:none">This was the first novel I've ever read in entirety in German so I was pretty proud of myself for that. However, it wasn't as good as I was hoping it would be. The back cover basically gives away the first 220 pages (of a 350 page book), so it was hard to get through the first 50% of the book already knowing what was going to happen. Needless to say, it was a slow start.<br /><br />Things I liked: great descriptions, different perspectives, good character development of Bert, Imke, and Merle.<br /><br />Things I disliked: the back cover gives most of the book away, Jette is way too dumb, huge plot holes, ends too quickly, lots of cliches.<br /><br />Perhaps it was the author's first book.</span>

<div id="review_24874757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24874757" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24874757?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=xx-creeped-me-out">xx-creeped-me-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=ser-wont-read-sequel">ser-wont-read-sequel</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer24874757&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24874757" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4880477309138557223">Listened to the audibook. Luckily. Would have taken me 10 times as long to read it myself because it would have bored me quickly.<br/><br/>Jette seems to be called Jenna in the English translation, haha. Pretty stupid if you consider that her name is somewhat important later on. As if English people couldn't deal with a German name. After all the whole story takes place in Germany.<br/><br/>The book has about 3 different points of view (Jette, Georg, the rest), therefore it is read by 3 different voices which is re</span>
  <span id="freeText4880477309138557223" style="display:none">Listened to the audibook. Luckily. Would have taken me 10 times as long to read it myself because it would have bored me quickly.<br /><br />Jette seems to be called Jenna in the English translation, haha. Pretty stupid if you consider that her name is somewhat important later on. As if English people couldn't deal with a German name. After all the whole story takes place in Germany.<br /><br />The book has about 3 different points of view (Jette, Georg, the rest), therefore it is read by 3 different voices which is refreshing. Change between the characters was enjoyable, prevented the story from getting too boring.<br /><br />Felt kind of old-fashioned sometimes. The girls had mobiles but they often had them turned off. Weird.<br /><br />You know who the murderer is right from the beginning. No chance to guess for yourself. Less suspense.<br /><br />I knew there were sequels of this book involving the main character Jette, therefore I wasn't afraid she'd get killed for one second. Even less suspense.<br /><br />Georg reminded me of the murderer from The Perfume a lot (aka too much). It is even mentioned that he read the book.<br /><br />If Jette loves Georg so much, why doesn't she try to talk to him when she realizes he's about to kill her? After all she still loves him in the last sentences.<br /><br />There are several obvious clues for Jette to draw the line between Caro's murderer and her own boyfriend. Annoyingly enough she just doesn't see them!<br /><br />That Jette's mom is a writer is an interesting aspect but also felt weird to me in several parts. It's probably always weird when a writer writes about a writer (especially when the author says that the fictional writer is fantastic at what she's doing).<br /><br />Caro's poems are crap. Not that bad but they're sure as hell not as awesome as all the characters in the book claim them to be. And no, Caro had no hidden talent for writing poetry -.-<br /><br />Some of the things mentioned seem unnecessary. Details about Bernd Melzig's past for example. The reader probably gets told about it, so s/he understands why and what Melzig thinks of the murderer. But if this is the purpose, the information is sold too cheaply.<br /><br />Sometimes things happen too easily to move the story forward. Unrealistic.<br /><br />Won't read (or listen to) the sequels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4880477309138557223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4450385898241761859" style="display:none"> * Jenna is a very young girl. Daughter of the famous book writer. She live with her two friends in a flat. Merle and Caro. Her parents are divorced. Even her mom is very wealthy, Jenna never depend on her mom for anything. Nathaniel, a strawberry picker. He is a very strange person, who only like woman who he think are like fairies. He is a lonely person. He like it that way. <br /> * Murders after murders, all had done it with the same motive. All those beautiful and innocent faces of those young girls. Laying there in the wood, lifeless. The police are now investigating but so far nothing seem to get them anywhere with this case. Caro, one of the victim, also was Jenna and Merle best friend. Jenna had promise to find Caro's murderer and revenge. One of the suspect person is Caro last boyfriend. The one that no one knows nothing about. Not even Caro know so much about him. Jenna and Merle are now in searching of him, but they had no idea how much danger they are in. Many had warn them about it, but they are too stubborn to listen. <br /> *This book was written to be read by teenagers. The author know that at this age many teen been experience love and broken hearts. So what the author trying to tell the readers is not to trust anyone. Get to know them first, cause you might never know what that person is really like on the inside. The author also wrote the book to warn teenagers not to put themselves into dangers. Also to teach teenagers that even words could put them in the most dangerous situation. In life unexpected things always happen. But every problem has a solution,so think about what you are gonna do to solve the problem first, before making any bad decision. <br /> * The theme of this book is to tell a person not to ever trust anyone. Also not to trust even the person that you you love, because that person one day might betray you. Also that even if you think you found the right person and that your relationship is going well. Think twice about it, because there will always be doubt in it. <br /> <br /> </span>

<div id="review_1329096212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1329096212" />
    <a title="Belinda Schön" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33026990-belinda-sch-n"><img alt="Belinda Schön" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421843161p2/33026990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1329096212?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belinda Schön" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belinda Schön" href="/user/show/33026990-belinda-sch-n">Belinda Schön</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1329096212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15200671720858729648">I am a huge lover of thriller-novels but this one just did not do it for me. We know who the murder is from the very beginning, and we follow his hunt for one of his last victim´s best friend. The mind of the killer was so messed up that it kept it interesting, yet, even at the end, there was no explanation for why he behaved this particular way and that was a huge dissapointment, because I wanted to know a little bit more about him. The main protagonist, Jette, went through a complete change of</span>
  <span id="freeText15200671720858729648" style="display:none">I am a huge lover of thriller-novels but this one just did not do it for me. We know who the murder is from the very beginning, and we follow his hunt for one of his last victim´s best friend. The mind of the killer was so messed up that it kept it interesting, yet, even at the end, there was no explanation for why he behaved this particular way and that was a huge dissapointment, because I wanted to know a little bit more about him. The main protagonist, Jette, went through a complete change of personality 5 minutes after meeting this guy. She became so annoying, and COME ON, no one inmediately falls in love with a tanned 30 year old man that paid for your books at a bookshop, specially since his appeareance and personality matches the one of the killer of your best friend 100% and you being an 18 year old girl. And no one made the connections, and this frustated me so much. The ending was too abrupt and I could not connect with the characters. The only thing I liked from the book was that the killer was slightly interesting to read about in order to discover his motives, etc. but the double perspective killed so much of this book. I can see why people liked this book but I could not overlook these details to make my reading experience more enjoyable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15200671720858729648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14291751719357325686" style="display:none">Jenna is 18 and on her own for the first time. She lives with Merle and Caro, two of her closest friends. When a young woman is found murdered, the girls are concerned but continue their lives. Then Caro goes missing and her body is found in the same way as the other three. Jenna and Merle are determined to find the murderer. Nate is sure he's been careful, but he's worried the police are on to him. Caro seemed like the perfect girl but she disappointed him. Now he has new prey...Jenna.<br /><br />The book was originally written in German then translated to English. <span id="freeTextContainer1517019042587154648">Monika Feth has written an intense page-turner in The Strawberry Picker. There are times that I forgot this is a young adults fiction. Although there isn't much suspense to the killer's identity, but I think the author has done a good job in creating the thrill especially towards the second half of the book where I find myself holding my breath and worrying for Jenna's safety. </span>

<div id="review_3201976636" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3201976636" />
    <a title="Isobel Ramsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40578112-isobel-ramsden"><img alt="Isobel Ramsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478284972p2/40578112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3201976636?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isobel Ramsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isobel Ramsden" href="/user/show/40578112-isobel-ramsden">Isobel Ramsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099488460" href="/book/show/923731.The_Strawberry_Picker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3201976636" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2265369771546851166">A compelling murder mystery set in Germany. You know who the murderer is from the beginning but the suspense centres on if/how the detective will catch him before he commits another one. Originally written in German, it's one of the rare YA books originally published in another language that has made it into English translation. And it's a good translation. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <span id="freeText1266470723554551783" style="display:none">What I disliked: <br />To be honest I hated the writing style<br /> God knows why but I just didn't like it. <br />Second the information that's been given at the backpack of the book takes place around page 200 and is literally the end of the book and the only thing you could have not guessed is how the outcome was. <br />So the reader didn't get anything new it's like you already know what's gonna happen because yes it's already written on the back. <br />Also there are some scenes where the characters said something that has already been said ten pages ago (I mean general information- what the characters like or disliked- I don't remember the scene) <br />What I liked:<br />The change of character perspective. It was pretty interesting to read and in the end you knew who was the main character. <br />(Even though I must admit it seemed like the writer changed the perspective to give it a little excitement because it was missing in the plot (just my point of view) )<br />Second I really enjoyed the characters. Everyone except for Caro. Maybe because I didn't like how they brought up that she harms herself and not really giving the reader any information about the disorder at all)<br />Still I loved - especially- the mom of the main character. I love how the writer works on their characters and how she shows them describing the places they live in. I loved the house. Even though I've never seen it I have such a perfect picture on my mind and that's something not many writers could make me imagine well. <br />And what I liked the most is how the 'small lovestory' between the mom and the police officer worked out because they worked out the perfect way. It was something small and it also made people realise you know what maybe you marriage isn't the same as it was but you should maybe try a little harder together and talk and spent time together instead of going and finding a new love especially if you're still married<br />It wasn't like all the other books I've read that just gave a fuck about that. And it really got on my nerves a little so it's pretty good that it worked out like that and hey you know they have kids ? <br />So yeessss <br />I still enjoyed reading it after I got used to a few things and it was a yes 3/6. A good book to kill time with on holidays </span>

<div id="review_724442564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724442564" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23481694-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594445700p2/23481694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724442564?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23481694-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099488460" href="/book/show/923731.The_Strawberry_Picker">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23481694-sarah?shelf=neutral">neutral</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724442564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16928105113745961121">Rating 3.5 stars. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the book. It was not as suspenseful as most mystery novels for the fact that it followed multiple characters, the murderer included. Yet, it was still interesting and took on a slower pace than I expected, but it was a pace that I liked and found intriguing. The POVs jumped around a bit, it may bug other people, for me I thought it was nicely played out. It has a flow to it that mends all the POVs together.<br/> <br/>The characters were interesting. Particularly the murderer. H</span>
  <span id="freeText16928105113745961121" style="display:none">Rating 3.5 stars. <br /><br />I enjoyed the book. It was not as suspenseful as most mystery novels for the fact that it followed multiple characters, the murderer included. Yet, it was still interesting and took on a slower pace than I expected, but it was a pace that I liked and found intriguing. The POVs jumped around a bit, it may bug other people, for me I thought it was nicely played out. It has a flow to it that mends all the POVs together.<br /> <br />The characters were interesting. Particularly the murderer. He had a unique motive to kill that was odd but compelling. Since the story follows his POV, right away you know who the murderer is and it gives you all his reasons for killing. The other characters had a personality, but I never felt a deep love or connection to them. But that’s beside the point, I’m sure most people read mystery books more for the mystery than the characters. In the end, the characters were just standard characters. <br /><br />The story is more about a murderer and his latest victim then a gripping mystery novel. Even the climax was dulled with the fact that the author skipped over it. Still, if you want a well written book that’s calmer than most, with an engrossing murderer, this book is a good choice. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16928105113745961121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5529059426855872709">This was my first time reading anything by a German author and I must say that the translation was flawless. I really believe that nothing was lost in the translation and it has made me want to read more by authors of different languages.<br/><br/>I found 'The Strawberry Picker' in the young adult section in the library but, to me, it didn't read like it was intended for a younger audience and could imagine adults of all ages enjoying it. <br/><br/>I enjoyed the way that the narrative was told because even though t</span>
  <span id="freeText5529059426855872709" style="display:none">This was my first time reading anything by a German author and I must say that the translation was flawless. I really believe that nothing was lost in the translation and it has made me want to read more by authors of different languages.<br /><br />I found 'The Strawberry Picker' in the young adult section in the library but, to me, it didn't read like it was intended for a younger audience and could imagine adults of all ages enjoying it. <br /><br />I enjoyed the way that the narrative was told because even though the first person protagonist was Jenna, the storyline wasn't presented in a bias way as we got to see all different viewpoints. <br /><br />The only down side of this book (and why I gave it 3/5 instead of 4) was that the end was kind of anti-climatic and the poor dog at the end was injured. :(<br /><br />Would really recommend it to people wanting to read a crime/suspense book.</span>

  <span id="freeText1706389542437350936" style="display:none">Jenna has finally managed to establish an independent life from her famous mother, sharing a flat with her friends Caro and Merle. The three girls are very different but their friendship is genuine. When Caro is murdered by a serial killer, Jenna and Merle decide to track him down and bring him to justice. Jenna's mother, a renowned author who writes crime novels, is horrified by this resolution and tries to stop their investigation, with little success, while the inspector assigned to the case is frustrated by the lack of leads. Meanwhile, Nathaniel, Caro's former boyfriend, has become intrigued by Jenna and is slowly weaving a spell of secrecy and sexual frustration over her.<br />The translation is very smooth and the novel is easy to read without being shallow or facile. It's a tense, chilling read, definitely recommended for people who love thrillers and psychological tension.</span>

The more intense the story got, the quicker point of views were changed... My only complaint was the text of the paperback format was very small and close together, I probably would have finished this a lot sooner if it hadn't been hard on my eyes...</span>

I think it's better to change point of views with only 2 views per chapter. Imke Thalheim's character was well too built than Jenna or Merle. I almost felt that she's </span>
  <span id="freeText6791420561487001363" style="display:none">Slow moving story. I can't believe that nothing spectacular came up at the storyline. Maybe the synopsis should have not revealed more. In addition, Feth didn't elaborate on details why there's a 7 stab and hair cut short. She also constantly changes the point of view that I need to breathe longer to set my mind for another angle. I think it's better to change point of views with only 2 views per chapter. Imke Thalheim's character was well too built than Jenna or Merle. I almost felt that she's the <i>ultimate</i> main character. But all is well. I'm not engrossed but I did not dislike. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7151679637879667544">This a translation of a title from Germany about older teen girls living together in an apartment & one of them is found dead, in the same manner as two other girls- there seems to be a serial killer on the loose! Her two roommates vow to find the killer, in spite of the risk, since he seems to be targeting girls of their age. Don't want to say more & spoil the story, quite suspenseful psychological fiction & a police procedural whodunnit. Liked the German setting- something a bit different!</span>

<div id="review_150028765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150028765" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/5014487-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150028765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6847892944419328214">When i started reading this thriller, I didn't know it was written for teenagers. Though, in the end, I didn't mind at all, because the only thing that indicated that during the read was the fact that the main character is a 18 year old girl. I really liked the writing style and the story was quite suspenseful although it was clear from the start who the murderer is. I also felt very touched by the emotions of the different characters and look forward reading more of Monika Feth.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rq/bmm7dqYkySj2Ga7BNUh1q5yn/oe1LcTjw052cJmhYvmVK3OS9BteNwSO8ExlaEMD2sbhGZQmjD4r+MxfkRQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AOUHcQKbygCM+04DsZLe585hnAH3/FUXXPyqmdtQMfse9LmhsKLej2k8sqZmMYrvw8uNmbAb3VWOy9C0ddvz1g==')})

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5583387417214391396">Ich wurde 1951 in Hagen in Westfalen geboren, einer Stadt zwischen Ruhrgebiet und Sauerland. Mit neunzehn bin ich nach Bonn gezogen und habe dort Germanistik und Anglistik studiert.<br/><br/>Bücher waren schon immer meine Leidenschaft, aber ich stamme aus einer Arbeiterfamilie (mein Vater war der erste, der an einem Schreibtisch arbeitete), in der Lesen als Luxus für reiche Leute galt. Deshalb habe ich mir </span>
  <span id="freeText5583387417214391396" style="display:none">Ich wurde 1951 in Hagen in Westfalen geboren, einer Stadt zwischen Ruhrgebiet und Sauerland. Mit neunzehn bin ich nach Bonn gezogen und habe dort Germanistik und Anglistik studiert.<br /><br />Bücher waren schon immer meine Leidenschaft, aber ich stamme aus einer Arbeiterfamilie (mein Vater war der erste, der an einem Schreibtisch arbeitete), in der Lesen als Luxus für reiche Leute galt. Deshalb habe ich mir Studienfächer ausgesucht, für die ich den ganzen Tag lesen, lesen und lesen durfte, ohne dass mich jemand fragte, ob ich nichts Vernünftiges zu tun hätte ...<br />Nach dem Studium habe ich mein erstes Buch geschrieben, ohne jemals zuvor auch nur eine einzige Zeile verfasst zu haben. Dass es tatsächlich gedruckt wurde und in einem großen Verlag erschien, kam mir vor wie ein Wunder.<br /><br />Eine Zeit lang habe ich als Journalistin gearbeitet. Doch die Lust am Bücherschreiben hat mich nicht mehr losgelassen und schließlich habe ich gewagt, mich ganz darauf einzulassen.<br /><br />Heute lebe ich als freiberufliche Schriftstellerin in einem kleinen Dorf in der Nähe von Köln. Ich schreibe Bücher für Kinder, Jugendliche und Erwachsene, arbeite für den Rundfunk und hin und wieder fürs Fernsehen.</span>
